I've uploaded a python code repository in the directory /testbed. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
The latest value, instead of the previous value,  is provided in $effect teardown if the state is a $derived
### Describe the bug

Not sure if this is a bug or intended. According to [this breaking change](https://github.com/sveltejs/svelte/pull/15469), if the state caused an $effect to rerun, Svelte should provide the previous value of the state in the teardown function. This work for $state currently, but not for $derived, though it does work if $derived is reassigned. 

### Reproduction

https://svelte.dev/playground/untitled?version=5.33.18#H4sIAAAAAAAACnWPy2rEMAxFf8WIgcl0woSuCm4SmC_oqqumizyU1tRVjKVkOgT_e3HS92MldHSPZM9A9TOChlsSIxY7SKE3Fhn03QxydnEWAaTvyaNzB57QSmRNzfgXbwcSJGHQkHPrjZOyokosimJVqA1LLZhc7q4_6II79GbCLuELXkZUyQb7HltJkp0qSjVHVEk7EA8WD3Z4SLaPRjFrtU0Vr5ZU4lFGT-qb9ENrzvjbC7GEXUV59vlsyptRZCA1UGtN-1TM617e70N57DrFebYmyv-z8X9XobyZ0J-8kXj7q-VK1mrmkGfurV36FUAKgi8CWvyI4T4FqY09GepA97VlDK_x94v_xwEAAA==

```shell
Svelte playground (5.33.18)
```

### Severity

annoyance
Incorrect prop value in onDestroy when there's a setter but not getter in the template
### Describe the bug

When a prop has a setter (for instance `<button onclick={() => (checked = !checked)}></button>`) but it doesn't have a getter (like `<p>{checked}</p>`), the value read during `onDestroy` does not match either the old or the current value of the prop, it's instead read as `null`.

This happens because the compiler decides to use `$.prop` to read the prop since it detects a "setter", `$.prop` "wraps" the prop in a `derived` but since we never read from it, when we execute `onDestroy` the `derived` is still in an "uninitialized" state hence it returns `null` instead of the correct value. 

### Reproduction

https://svelte.dev/playground/4fa745c18a3c41e88bda761f37b36783?version=5.34.9

Click `count++` twice, the 2nd time the `Component` is unmounted and `onDestroy` is called and it will log the incorrect `checked` value that should be `true` but is logged as `null`.

    46	/**
    47	 * @param {'$effect' | '$effect.pre' | '$inspect'} rune
    48	 */
    49	export function validate_effect(rune) {
    50	        if (active_effect === null && active_reaction === null) {
    51	                e.effect_orphan(rune);
    52	        }
    53	
    54	        if (active_reaction !== null && (active_reaction.f & UNOWNED) !== 0 && active_effect === null) {
    55	                e.effect_in_unowned_derived();
    56	        }
    57	
    58	        if (is_destroying_effect) {
    59	                e.effect_in_teardown(rune);
    60	        }
    61	}

    63	/**
    64	 * @param {Effect} effect
    65	 * @param {Effect} parent_effect
    66	 */
    67	function push_effect(effect, parent_effect) {
    68	        var parent_last = parent_effect.last;
    69	        if (parent_last === null) {
    70	                parent_effect.last = parent_effect.first = effect;
    71	        } else {
    72	                parent_last.next = effect;
    73	                effect.prev = parent_last;
    74	                parent_effect.last = effect;
    75	        }
    76	}
    77	
    78	/**
    79	 * @param {number} type
    80	 * @param {null | (() => void | (() => void))} fn
    81	 * @param {boolean} sync
    82	 * @param {boolean} push
    83	 * @returns {Effect}
    84	 */
    85	function create_effect(type, fn, sync, push = true) {
    86	        var parent = active_effect;
    87	
    88	        if (DEV) {
    89	                // Ensure the parent is never an inspect effect
    90	                while (parent !== null && (parent.f & INSPECT_EFFECT) !== 0) {
    91	                        parent = parent.parent;
    92	                }
    93	        }
    94	
    95	        /** @type {Effect} */
    96	        var effect = {
    97	                ctx: component_context,
    98	                deps: null,
    99	                nodes_start: null,
   100	                nodes_end: null,
   101	                f: type | DIRTY,
   102	                first: null,
   103	                fn,
   104	                last: null,
   105	                next: null,
   106	                parent,
   107	                prev: null,
   108	                teardown: null,
   109	                transitions: null,
   110	                wv: 0,
   111	                ac: null
   112	        };
   113	
   114	        if (DEV) {
   115	                effect.component_function = dev_current_component_function;
   116	        }
   117	
   118	        if (sync) {
   119	                try {
   120	                        update_effect(effect);
   121	                        effect.f |= EFFECT_RAN;
   122	                } catch (e) {
   123	                        destroy_effect(effect);
   124	                        throw e;
   125	                }
   126	        } else if (fn !== null) {
   127	                schedule_effect(effect);
   128	        }
   129	
   130	        // if an effect has no dependencies, no DOM and no teardown function,
   131	        // don't bother adding it to the effect tree
   132	        var inert =
   133	                sync &&
   134	                effect.deps === null &&
   135	                effect.first === null &&
   136	                effect.nodes_start === null &&
   137	                effect.teardown === null &&
   138	                (effect.f & (EFFECT_HAS_DERIVED | BOUNDARY_EFFECT)) === 0;
   139	
   140	        if (!inert && push) {
   141	                if (parent !== null) {
   142	                        push_effect(effect, parent);
   143	                }
   144	
   145	                // if we're in a derived, add the effect there too
   146	                if (active_reaction !== null && (active_reaction.f & DERIVED) !== 0) {
   147	                        var derived = /** @type {Derived} */ (active_reaction);
   148	                        (derived.effects ??= []).push(effect);
   149	                }
   150	        }
   151	
   152	        return effect;
   153	}

   159	export function effect_tracking() {

   177	export function user_effect(fn) {
   178	        validate_effect('$effect');
   179	
   180	        // Non-nested `$effect(...)` in a component should be deferred
   181	        // until the component is mounted
   182	        var defer =
   183	                active_effect !== null &&
   184	                (active_effect.f & BRANCH_EFFECT) !== 0 &&
   185	                component_context !== null &&

   195	                var context = /** @type {ComponentContext} */ (component_context);
   196	                (context.e ??= []).push({
   197	                        fn,
   198	                        effect: active_effect,
   199	                        reaction: active_reaction
   200	                });
   201	        } else {
   202	                var signal = effect(fn);
   203	                return signal;

   232	export function effect_root(fn) {

   240	/**
   241	 * An effect root whose children can transition out
   242	 * @param {() => void} fn
   243	 * @returns {(options?: { outro?: boolean }) => Promise<void>}

   245	export function component_root(fn) {
   246	        const effect = create_effect(ROOT_EFFECT, fn, true);
   247	
   248	        return (options = {}) => {
   249	                return new Promise((fulfil) => {
   250	                        if (options.outro) {
   251	                                pause_effect(effect, () => {
   252	                                        destroy_effect(effect);
   253	                                        fulfil(undefined);
   254	                                });
   255	                        } else {
   256	                                destroy_effect(effect);
   257	                                fulfil(undefined);
   258	                        }
   259	                });
   260	        };
   261	}

   271	/**
   272	 * Internal representation of `$: ..`
   273	 * @param {() => any} deps
   274	 * @param {() => void | (() => void)} fn
   275	 */
   276	export function legacy_pre_effect(deps, fn) {
   277	        var context = /** @type {ComponentContextLegacy} */ (component_context);
   278	
   279	        /** @type {{ effect: null | Effect, ran: boolean }} */
   280	        var token = { effect: null, ran: false };
   281	        context.l.r1.push(token);
   282	
   283	        token.effect = render_effect(() => {
   284	                deps();
   285	
   286	                // If this legacy pre effect has already run before the end of the reset, then
   287	                // bail out to emulate the same behavior.
   288	                if (token.ran) return;
   289	
   290	                token.ran = true;
   291	                set(context.l.r2, true);
   292	                untrack(fn);
   293	        });
   294	}
   295	
   296	export function legacy_pre_effect_reset() {
   297	        var context = /** @type {ComponentContextLegacy} */ (component_context);
   298	
   299	        render_effect(() => {
   300	                if (!get(context.l.r2)) return;
   301	
   302	                // Run dirty `$:` statements
   303	                for (var token of context.l.r1) {
   304	                        var effect = token.effect;
   305	
   306	                        // If the effect is CLEAN, then make it MAYBE_DIRTY. This ensures we traverse through
   307	                        // the effects dependencies and correctly ensure each dependency is up-to-date.
   308	                        if ((effect.f & CLEAN) !== 0) {
   309	                                set_signal_status(effect, MAYBE_DIRTY);
   310	                        }
   311	
   312	                        if (check_dirtiness(effect)) {
   313	                                update_effect(effect);
   314	                        }
   315	
   316	                        token.ran = false;
   317	                }
   318	
   319	                context.l.r2.v = false; // set directly to avoid rerunning this effect
   320	        });
   321	}
   322	
   323	/**
   324	 * @param {() => void | (() => void)} fn
   325	 * @returns {Effect}

   327	export function render_effect(fn) {
   328	        return create_effect(RENDER_EFFECT, fn, true);

   330	
   331	/**
   332	 * @param {(...expressions: any) => void | (() => void)} fn
   333	 * @param {Array<() => any>} thunks
   334	 * @param {<T>(fn: () => T) => Derived<T>} d
   335	 * @returns {Effect}
   336	 */
   337	export function template_effect(fn, thunks = [], d = derived) {
   338	        if (DEV) {
   339	                // wrap the effect so that we can decorate stack trace with `in {expression}`
   340	                // (TODO maybe there's a better approach?)
   341	                return render_effect(() => {
   342	                        var outer = /** @type {Effect} */ (active_effect);
   343	                        var inner = () => fn(...deriveds.map(get));
   344	
   345	                        define_property(outer.fn, 'name', { value: '{expression}' });
   346	                        define_property(inner, 'name', { value: '{expression}' });
   347	
   348	                        const deriveds = thunks.map(d);
   349	                        block(inner);
   350	                });
   351	        }
   352	
   353	        const deriveds = thunks.map(d);
   354	        return block(() => fn(...deriveds.map(get)));
   355	}
   356	
   357	/**
   358	 * @param {(() => void)} fn
   359	 * @param {number} flags
   360	 */
   361	export function block(fn, flags = 0) {
   362	        var effect = create_effect(RENDER_EFFECT | BLOCK_EFFECT | flags, fn, true);
   363	        if (DEV) {
   364	                effect.dev_stack = dev_stack;
   365	        }
   366	        return effect;
   367	}

   371	 * @param {boolean} [push]

   373	export function branch(fn, push = true) {

   375	}
   376	
   377	/**
   378	 * @param {Effect} effect
   379	 */
   380	export function execute_effect_teardown(effect) {
   381	        var teardown = effect.teardown;
   382	        if (teardown !== null) {
   383	                const previously_destroying_effect = is_destroying_effect;
   384	                const previous_reaction = active_reaction;
   385	                set_is_destroying_effect(true);
   386	                set_active_reaction(null);
   387	                try {
   388	                        teardown.call(null);
   389	                } finally {
   390	                        set_is_destroying_effect(previously_destroying_effect);
   391	                        set_active_reaction(previous_reaction);
   392	                }
   393	        }
   394	}
   395	
   396	/**
   397	 * @param {Effect} signal
   398	 * @param {boolean} remove_dom
   399	 * @returns {void}
   400	 */
   401	export function destroy_effect_children(signal, remove_dom = false) {
   402	        var effect = signal.first;
   403	        signal.first = signal.last = null;
   404	
   405	        while (effect !== null) {
   406	                effect.ac?.abort(STALE_REACTION);
   407	
   408	                var next = effect.next;
   409	
   410	                if ((effect.f & ROOT_EFFECT) !== 0) {
   411	                        // this is now an independent root
   412	                        effect.parent = null;
   413	                } else {
   414	                        destroy_effect(effect, remove_dom);
   415	                }
   416	
   417	                effect = next;
   418	        }
   419	}
   420	
   421	/**
   422	 * @param {Effect} signal
   423	 * @returns {void}
   424	 */
   425	export function destroy_block_effect_children(signal) {
   426	        var effect = signal.first;
   427	
   428	        while (effect !== null) {
   429	                var next = effect.next;
   430	                if ((effect.f & BRANCH_EFFECT) === 0) {
   431	                        destroy_effect(effect);
   432	                }
   433	                effect = next;
   434	        }
   435	}
   436	
   437	/**
   438	 * @param {Effect} effect
   439	 * @param {boolean} [remove_dom]
   440	 * @returns {void}
   441	 */
   442	export function destroy_effect(effect, remove_dom = true) {
   443	        var removed = false;
   444	
   445	        if (
   446	                (remove_dom || (effect.f & HEAD_EFFECT) !== 0) &&
   447	                effect.nodes_start !== null &&
   448	                effect.nodes_end !== null
   449	        ) {
   450	                remove_effect_dom(effect.nodes_start, /** @type {TemplateNode} */ (effect.nodes_end));
   451	                removed = true;
   452	        }
   453	
   454	        destroy_effect_children(effect, remove_dom && !removed);
   455	        remove_reactions(effect, 0);
   456	        set_signal_status(effect, DESTROYED);
   457	
   458	        var transitions = effect.transitions;
   459	
   460	        if (transitions !== null) {
   461	                for (const transition of transitions) {
   462	                        transition.stop();
   463	                }
   464	        }
   465	
   466	        execute_effect_teardown(effect);
   467	
   468	        var parent = effect.parent;
   469	
   470	        // If the parent doesn't have any children, then skip this work altogether
   471	        if (parent !== null && parent.first !== null) {
   472	                unlink_effect(effect);
   473	        }
   474	
   475	        if (DEV) {
   476	                effect.component_function = null;
   477	        }
   478	
   479	        // `first` and `child` are nulled out in destroy_effect_children
   480	        // we don't null out `parent` so that error propagation can work correctly
   481	        effect.next =
   482	                effect.prev =
   483	                effect.teardown =
   484	                effect.ctx =
   485	                effect.deps =
   486	                effect.fn =
   487	                effect.nodes_start =
   488	                effect.nodes_end =
   489	                effect.ac =
   490	                        null;
   491	}
   492	
   493	/**
   494	 *
   495	 * @param {TemplateNode | null} node
   496	 * @param {TemplateNode} end
   497	 */
   498	export function remove_effect_dom(node, end) {
   499	        while (node !== null) {
   500	                /** @type {TemplateNode | null} */
   501	                var next = node === end ? null : /** @type {TemplateNode} */ (get_next_sibling(node));
   502	
   503	                node.remove();
   504	                node = next;
   505	        }
   506	}
   507	
   508	/**
   509	 * Detach an effect from the effect tree, freeing up memory and
   510	 * reducing the amount of work that happens on subsequent traversals
   511	 * @param {Effect} effect
   512	 */
   513	export function unlink_effect(effect) {
   514	        var parent = effect.parent;
   515	        var prev = effect.prev;
   516	        var next = effect.next;
   517	
   518	        if (prev !== null) prev.next = next;
   519	        if (next !== null) next.prev = prev;
   520	
   521	        if (parent !== null) {
   522	                if (parent.first === effect) parent.first = next;
   523	                if (parent.last === effect) parent.last = prev;
   524	        }
   525	}
   526	
   527	/**
   528	 * When a block effect is removed, we don't immediately destroy it or yank it
   529	 * out of the DOM, because it might have transitions. Instead, we 'pause' it.
   530	 * It stays around (in memory, and in the DOM) until outro transitions have
   531	 * completed, and if the state change is reversed then we _resume_ it.
   532	 * A paused effect does not update, and the DOM subtree becomes inert.
   533	 * @param {Effect} effect
   534	 * @param {() => void} [callback]
   535	 */
   536	export function pause_effect(effect, callback) {
   537	        /** @type {TransitionManager[]} */
   538	        var transitions = [];
   539	
   540	        pause_children(effect, transitions, true);
   541	
   542	        run_out_transitions(transitions, () => {
   543	                destroy_effect(effect);
   544	                if (callback) callback();
   545	        });
   546	}
   547	
   548	/**
   549	 * @param {TransitionManager[]} transitions
   550	 * @param {() => void} fn
   551	 */
   552	export function run_out_transitions(transitions, fn) {
   553	        var remaining = transitions.length;
   554	        if (remaining > 0) {
   555	                var check = () => --remaining || fn();
   556	                for (var transition of transitions) {
   557	                        transition.out(check);
   558	                }
   559	        } else {
   560	                fn();
   561	        }
   562	}
   563	
   564	/**
   565	 * @param {Effect} effect
   566	 * @param {TransitionManager[]} transitions
   567	 * @param {boolean} local
   568	 */
   569	export function pause_children(effect, transitions, local) {
   570	        if ((effect.f & INERT) !== 0) return;
   571	        effect.f ^= INERT;
   572	
   573	        if (effect.transitions !== null) {
   574	                for (const transition of effect.transitions) {
   575	                        if (transition.is_global || local) {
   576	                                transitions.push(transition);
   577	                        }
   578	                }
   579	        }
   580	
   581	        var child = effect.first;
   582	
   583	        while (child !== null) {
   584	                var sibling = child.next;
   585	                var transparent = (child.f & EFFECT_TRANSPARENT) !== 0 || (child.f & BRANCH_EFFECT) !== 0;
   586	                // TODO we don't need to call pause_children recursively with a linked list in place
   587	                // it's slightly more involved though as we have to account for `transparent` changing
   588	                // through the tree.
   589	                pause_children(child, transitions, transparent ? local : false);
   590	                child = sibling;
   591	        }
   592	}
   593	
   594	/**
   595	 * The opposite of `pause_effect`. We call this if (for example)
   596	 * `x` becomes falsy then truthy: `{#if x}...{/if}`
   597	 * @param {Effect} effect
   598	 */
   599	export function resume_effect(effect) {
   600	        resume_children(effect, true);
   601	}
   602	
   603	/**
   604	 * @param {Effect} effect
   605	 * @param {boolean} local
   606	 */
   607	function resume_children(effect, local) {
   608	        if ((effect.f & INERT) === 0) return;
   609	        effect.f ^= INERT;
   610	
   611	        var child = effect.first;
   612	
   613	        while (child !== null) {
   614	                var sibling = child.next;
   615	                var transparent = (child.f & EFFECT_TRANSPARENT) !== 0 || (child.f & BRANCH_EFFECT) !== 0;
   616	                // TODO we don't need to call resume_children recursively with a linked list in place
   617	                // it's slightly more involved though as we have to account for `transparent` changing
   618	                // through the tree.
   619	                resume_children(child, transparent ? local : false);
   620	                child = sibling;
   621	        }
   622	
   623	        if (effect.transitions !== null) {
   624	                for (const transition of effect.transitions) {
   625	                        if (transition.is_global || local) {
   626	                                transition.in();
   627	                        }
   628	                }
   629	        }
   630	}
   631

   116	/**
   117	 * @param {Derived} derived
   118	 * @returns {Effect | null}
   119	 */
   120	function get_derived_parent_effect(derived) {
   121	        var parent = derived.parent;
   122	        while (parent !== null) {
   123	                if ((parent.f & DERIVED) === 0) {
   124	                        return /** @type {Effect} */ (parent);
   125	                }
   126	                parent = parent.parent;
   127	        }
   128	        return null;
   129	}
   130	
   131	/**
   132	 * @template T
   133	 * @param {Derived} derived
   134	 * @returns {T}
   135	 */
   136	export function execute_derived(derived) {
   137	        var value;
   138	        var prev_active_effect = active_effect;
   139	
   140	        set_active_effect(get_derived_parent_effect(derived));
   141	
   142	        if (DEV) {
   143	                let prev_inspect_effects = inspect_effects;
   144	                set_inspect_effects(new Set());
   145	                try {
   146	                        if (stack.includes(derived)) {
   147	                                e.derived_references_self();
   148	                        }
   149	
   150	                        stack.push(derived);
   151	
   152	                        destroy_derived_effects(derived);
   153	                        value = update_reaction(derived);
   154	                } finally {
   155	                        set_active_effect(prev_active_effect);
   156	                        set_inspect_effects(prev_inspect_effects);
   157	                        stack.pop();
   158	                }
   159	        } else {
   160	                try {
   161	                        destroy_derived_effects(derived);
   162	                        value = update_reaction(derived);
   163	                } finally {
   164	                        set_active_effect(prev_active_effect);
   165	                }
   166	        }
   167	
   168	        return value;
   169	}
   170	
   171	/**
   172	 * @param {Derived} derived
   173	 * @returns {void}
   174	 */
   175	export function update_derived(derived) {
   176	        var value = execute_derived(derived);
   177	
   178	        if (!derived.equals(value)) {
   179	                derived.v = value;
   180	                derived.wv = increment_write_version();
   181	        }
   182	
   183	        // don't mark derived clean if we're reading it inside a
   184	        // cleanup function, or it will cache a stale value
   185	        if (is_destroying_effect) return;
   186	
   187	        var status =
   188	                (skip_reaction || (derived.f & UNOWNED) !== 0) && derived.deps !== null ? MAYBE_DIRTY : CLEAN;
   189	
   190	        set_signal_status(derived, status);
   191	}

   115	 * Tracks writes that the effect it's executed in doesn't listen to yet,
   116	 * so that the dependency can be added to the effect later on if it then reads it
   117	 * @type {null | Source[]}
   118	 */
   119	export let untracked_writes = null;
   120	
   121	/** @param {null | Source[]} value */
   122	export function set_untracked_writes(value) {
   123	        untracked_writes = value;
   124	}
   125	
   126	/**
   127	 * @type {number} Used by sources and deriveds for handling updates.
   128	 * Version starts from 1 so that unowned deriveds differentiate between a created effect and a run one for tracing
   129	 **/
   130	let write_version = 1;
   131	
   132	/** @type {number} Used to version each read of a source of derived to avoid duplicating depedencies inside a reaction */
   133	let read_version = 0;
   134	
   135	// If we are working with a get() chain that has no active container,
   136	// to prevent memory leaks, we skip adding the reaction.
   137	export let skip_reaction = false;
   138	// Handle collecting all signals which are read during a specific time frame
   139	/** @type {Set<Value> | null} */
   140	export let captured_signals = null;
   141	
   142	/** @param {Set<Value> | null} value */
   143	export function set_captured_signals(value) {
   144	        captured_signals = value;
   145	}
   146	
   147	export function increment_write_version() {
   148	        return ++write_version;
   149	}
   150	
   151	/**
   152	 * Determines whether a derived or effect is dirty.
   153	 * If it is MAYBE_DIRTY, will set the status to CLEAN
   154	 * @param {Reaction} reaction
   155	 * @returns {boolean}
   156	 */
   157	export function check_dirtiness(reaction) {
   158	        var flags = reaction.f;
   159	
   160	        if ((flags & DIRTY) !== 0) {
   161	                return true;
   162	        }
   163	
   164	        if ((flags & MAYBE_DIRTY) !== 0) {
   165	                var dependencies = reaction.deps;
   166	                var is_unowned = (flags & UNOWNED) !== 0;
   167	
   168	                if (dependencies !== null) {
   169	                        var i;
   170	                        var dependency;
   171	                        var is_disconnected = (flags & DISCONNECTED) !== 0;
   172	                        var is_unowned_connected = is_unowned && active_effect !== null && !skip_reaction;
   173	                        var length = dependencies.length;
   174	
   175	                        // If we are working with a disconnected or an unowned signal that is now connected (due to an active effect)
   176	                        // then we need to re-connect the reaction to the dependency
   177	                        if (is_disconnected || is_unowned_connected) {
   178	                                var derived = /** @type {Derived} */ (reaction);
   179	                                var parent = derived.parent;
   180	
   181	                                for (i = 0; i < length; i++) {
   182	                                        dependency = dependencies[i];
   183	
   184	                                        // We always re-add all reactions (even duplicates) if the derived was
   185	                                        // previously disconnected, however we don't if it was unowned as we
   186	                                        // de-duplicate dependencies in that case
   187	                                        if (is_disconnected || !dependency?.reactions?.includes(derived)) {
   188	                                                (dependency.reactions ??= []).push(derived);
   189	                                        }
   190	                                }
   191	
   192	                                if (is_disconnected) {
   193	                                        derived.f ^= DISCONNECTED;
   194	                                }
   195	                                // If the unowned derived is now fully connected to the graph again (it's unowned and reconnected, has a parent
   196	                                // and the parent is not unowned), then we can mark it as connected again, removing the need for the unowned
   197	                                // flag
   198	                                if (is_unowned_connected && parent !== null && (parent.f & UNOWNED) === 0) {
   199	                                        derived.f ^= UNOWNED;
   200	                                }
   201	                        }
   202	
   203	                        for (i = 0; i < length; i++) {
   204	                                dependency = dependencies[i];
   205	
   206	                                if (check_dirtiness(/** @type {Derived} */ (dependency))) {
   207	                                        update_derived(/** @type {Derived} */ (dependency));
   208	                                }
   209	
   210	                                if (dependency.wv > reaction.wv) {
   211	                                        return true;
   212	                                }
   213	                        }
   214	                }
   215	
   216	                // Unowned signals should never be marked as clean unless they
   217	                // are used within an active_effect without skip_reaction
   218	                if (!is_unowned || (active_effect !== null && !skip_reaction)) {
   219	                        set_signal_status(reaction, CLEAN);
   220	                }
   221	        }
   222	
   223	        return false;
   224	}
   225	
   226	/**
   227	 * @param {Value} signal
   228	 * @param {Effect} effect
   229	 * @param {boolean} [root]
   230	 */
   231	function schedule_possible_effect_self_invalidation(signal, effect, root = true) {
   232	        var reactions = signal.reactions;
   233	        if (reactions === null) return;
   234	
   235	        for (var i = 0; i < reactions.length; i++) {
   236	                var reaction = reactions[i];
   237	
   238	                if (reaction_sources?.[1].includes(signal) && reaction_sources[0] === active_reaction) continue;
   239	
   240	                if ((reaction.f & DERIVED) !== 0) {
   241	                        schedule_possible_effect_self_invalidation(/** @type {Derived} */ (reaction), effect, false);
   242	                } else if (effect === reaction) {
   243	                        if (root) {
   244	                                set_signal_status(reaction, DIRTY);
   245	                        } else if ((reaction.f & CLEAN) !== 0) {
   246	                                set_signal_status(reaction, MAYBE_DIRTY);
   247	                        }
   248	                        schedule_effect(/** @type {Effect} */ (reaction));
   249	                }
   250	        }
   251	}

   369	/**
   370	 * @template V
   371	 * @param {Reaction} signal
   372	 * @param {Value<V>} dependency
   373	 * @returns {void}
   374	 */
   375	function remove_reaction(signal, dependency) {
   376	        let reactions = dependency.reactions;
   377	        if (reactions !== null) {
   378	                var index = index_of.call(reactions, signal);
   379	                if (index !== -1) {
   380	                        var new_length = reactions.length - 1;
   381	                        if (new_length === 0) {
   382	                                reactions = dependency.reactions = null;
   383	                        } else {
   384	                                // Swap with last element and then remove.
   385	                                reactions[index] = reactions[new_length];
   386	                                reactions.pop();
   387	                        }
   388	                }
   389	        }
   390	        // If the derived has no reactions, then we can disconnect it from the graph,
   391	        // allowing it to either reconnect in the future, or be GC'd by the VM.
   392	        if (
   393	                reactions === null &&
   394	                (dependency.f & DERIVED) !== 0 &&
   395	                // Destroying a child effect while updating a parent effect can cause a dependency to appear
   396	                // to be unused, when in fact it is used by the currently-updating parent. Checking `new_deps`
   397	                // allows us to skip the expensive work of disconnecting and immediately reconnecting it
   398	                (new_deps === null || !new_deps.includes(dependency))
   399	        ) {
   400	                set_signal_status(dependency, MAYBE_DIRTY);
   401	                // If we are working with a derived that is owned by an effect, then mark it as being
   402	                // disconnected.
   403	                if ((dependency.f & (UNOWNED | DISCONNECTED)) === 0) {
   404	                        dependency.f ^= DISCONNECTED;
   405	                }
   406	                // Disconnect any reactions owned by this reaction
   407	                destroy_derived_effects(/** @type {Derived} **/ (dependency));
   408	                remove_reactions(/** @type {Derived} **/ (dependency), 0);
   409	        }
   410	}

   412	/**
   413	 * @param {Reaction} signal
   414	 * @param {number} start_index
   415	 * @returns {void}

   417	export function remove_reactions(signal, start_index) {
   418	        var dependencies = signal.deps;
   419	        if (dependencies === null) return;
   420	
   421	        for (var i = start_index; i < dependencies.length; i++) {

   426	/**
   427	 * @param {Effect} effect
   428	 * @returns {void}
   429	 */
   430	export function update_effect(effect) {
   431	        var flags = effect.f;
   432	
   433	        if ((flags & DESTROYED) !== 0) {
   434	                return;
   435	        }
   436	
   437	        set_signal_status(effect, CLEAN);
   438	
   439	        var previous_effect = active_effect;
   440	        var was_updating_effect = is_updating_effect;

   443	        is_updating_effect = true;
   444	
   445	        if (DEV) {
   446	                var previous_component_fn = dev_current_component_function;

   449	                // only block effects have a dev stack, keep the current one otherwise

   451	        }

   455	                        destroy_block_effect_children(effect);
   456	                } else {
   457	                        destroy_effect_children(effect);
   458	                }

   460	                execute_effect_teardown(effect);
   461	                var teardown = update_reaction(effect);

   463	                effect.wv = write_version;
   464	
   465	                // In DEV, increment versions of any sources that were written to during the effect,
   466	                // so that they are correctly marked as dirty when the effect re-runs
   467	                if (DEV && tracing_mode_flag && (effect.f & DIRTY) !== 0 && effect.deps !== null) {

   570	function flush_queued_effects(effects) {
   571	        var length = effects.length;
   572	        if (length === 0) return;

   574	        for (var i = 0; i < length; i++) {

   624	
   625	/**
   626	 *
   627	 * This function both runs render effects and collects user effects in topological order
   628	 * from the starting effect passed in. Effects will be collected when they match the filtered
   629	 * bitwise flag passed in only. The collected effects array will be populated with all the user
   630	 * effects to be flushed.
   631	 *
   632	 * @param {Effect} root
   633	 * @returns {Effect[]}
   634	 */
   635	function process_effects(root) {
   636	        /** @type {Effect[]} */
   637	        var effects = [];
   638	
   639	        /** @type {Effect | null} */
   640	        var effect = root;
   641	
   642	        while (effect !== null) {
   643	                var flags = effect.f;
   644	                var is_branch = (flags & (BRANCH_EFFECT | ROOT_EFFECT)) !== 0;
   645	                var is_skippable_branch = is_branch && (flags & CLEAN) !== 0;
   646	
   647	                if (!is_skippable_branch && (flags & INERT) === 0) {
   648	                        if ((flags & EFFECT) !== 0) {
   649	                                effects.push(effect);
   650	                        } else if (is_branch) {
   651	                                effect.f ^= CLEAN;
   652	                        } else {
   653	                                if (check_dirtiness(effect)) {
   654	                                        update_effect(effect);
   655	                                }
   656	                        }
   657	
   658	                        /** @type {Effect | null} */
   659	                        var child = effect.first;
   660	
   661	                        if (child !== null) {
   662	                                effect = child;
   663	                                continue;
   664	                        }
   665	                }
   666	
   667	                var parent = effect.parent;
   668	                effect = effect.next;
   669	
   670	                while (effect === null && parent !== null) {
   671	                        effect = parent.next;
   672	                        parent = parent.parent;
   673	                }
   674	        }
   675	
   676	        return effects;
   677	}
   678	
   679	/**
   680	 * Synchronously flush any pending updates.
   681	 * Returns void if no callback is provided, otherwise returns the result of calling the callback.
   682	 * @template [T=void]
   683	 * @param {(() => T) | undefined} [fn]
   684	 * @returns {T}
   685	 */
   686	export function flushSync(fn) {
   687	        var result;
   688	
   689	        if (fn) {
   690	                is_flushing = true;
   691	                flush_queued_root_effects();
   692	
   693	                is_flushing = true;
   694	                result = fn();
   695	        }
   696	
   697	        while (true) {
   698	                flush_tasks();
   699	
   700	                if (queued_root_effects.length === 0) {

   732	export function get(signal) {
   733	        var flags = signal.f;
   734	        var is_derived = (flags & DERIVED) !== 0;
   735	
   736	        if (captured_signals !== null) {
   737	                captured_signals.add(signal);
   738	        }
   739	
   740	        // Register the dependency on the current reaction signal.
   741	        if (active_reaction !== null && !untracking) {
   742	                if (!reaction_sources?.[1].includes(signal) || reaction_sources[0] !== active_reaction) {
   743	                        var deps = active_reaction.deps;
   744	                        if (signal.rv < read_version) {
   745	                                signal.rv = read_version;
   746	                                // If the signal is accessing the same dependencies in the same
   747	                                // order as it did last time, increment `skipped_deps`
   748	                                // rather than updating `new_deps`, which creates GC cost
   749	                                if (new_deps === null && deps !== null && deps[skipped_deps] === signal) {
   750	                                        skipped_deps++;
   751	                                } else if (new_deps === null) {
   752	                                        new_deps = [signal];
   753	                                } else if (!skip_reaction || !new_deps.includes(signal)) {
   754	                                        // Normally we can push duplicated dependencies to `new_deps`, but if we're inside
   755	                                        // an unowned derived because skip_reaction is true, then we need to ensure that
   756	                                        // we don't have duplicates
   757	                                        new_deps.push(signal);
   758	                                }
   759	                        }
   760	                }
   761	        } else if (
   762	                is_derived &&
   763	                /** @type {Derived} */ (signal).deps === null &&
   764	                /** @type {Derived} */ (signal).effects === null
   765	        ) {
   766	                var derived = /** @type {Derived} */ (signal);
   767	                var parent = derived.parent;
   768	
   769	                if (parent !== null && (parent.f & UNOWNED) === 0) {
   770	                        // If the derived is owned by another derived then mark it as unowned
   771	                        // as the derived value might have been referenced in a different context
   772	                        // since and thus its parent might not be its true owner anymore
   773	                        derived.f ^= UNOWNED;
   774	                }
   775	        }
   776	
   777	        if (is_derived) {
   778	                derived = /** @type {Derived} */ (signal);
   779	
   780	                if (check_dirtiness(derived)) {
   781	                        update_derived(derived);
   782	                }
   783	        }
   784	
   785	        if (
   786	                DEV &&
   787	                tracing_mode_flag &&
   788	                !untracking &&
   789	                tracing_expressions !== null &&
   790	                active_reaction !== null &&
   791	                tracing_expressions.reaction === active_reaction
   792	        ) {
   793	                // Used when mapping state between special blocks like `each`
   794	                if (signal.trace) {
   795	                        signal.trace();
   796	                } else {
   797	                        var trace = get_stack('TracedAt');
   798	
   799	                        if (trace) {
   800	                                var entry = tracing_expressions.entries.get(signal);
   801	
   802	                                if (entry === undefined) {
   803	                                        entry = { traces: [] };
   804	                                        tracing_expressions.entries.set(signal, entry);
   805	                                }
   806	
   807	                                var last = entry.traces[entry.traces.length - 1];
   808	
   809	                                // traces can be duplicated, e.g. by `snapshot` invoking both
   810	                                // both `getOwnPropertyDescriptor` and `get` traps at once
   811	                                if (trace.stack !== last?.stack) {
   812	                                        entry.traces.push(trace);
   813	                                }
   814	                        }
   815	                }
   816	        }
   817	
   818	        if (is_destroying_effect && old_values.has(signal)) {
   819	                return old_values.get(signal);
   820	        }
   821	
   822	        return signal.v;
   823	}
   824	
   825	/**
   826	 * Like `get`, but checks for `undefined`. Used for `var` declarations because they can be accessed before being declared
   827	 * @template V
   828	 * @param {Value<V> | undefined} signal
   829	 * @returns {V | undefined}
   830	 */
   831	export function safe_get(signal) {
   832	        return signal && get(signal);
   833	}

   136	        if (
   137	                active_reaction !== null &&

   139	                // to ensure we error if state is set inside an inspect effect

   157	/**
   158	 * @template V
   159	 * @param {Source<V>} source
   160	 * @param {V} value
   161	 * @returns {V}

   163	export function internal_set(source, value) {
   164	        if (!source.equals(value)) {
   165	                var old_value = source.v;
   166	
   167	                if (is_destroying_effect) {
   168	                        old_values.set(source, value);
   169	                } else {
   170	                        old_values.set(source, old_value);
   171	                }
   172	
   173	                source.v = value;
   174	
   175	                if (DEV && tracing_mode_flag) {
   176	                        source.updated = get_stack('UpdatedAt');
   177	
   178	                        if (active_effect !== null) {
   179	                                source.set_during_effect = true;
   180	                        }
   181	                }
   182	
   183	                if ((source.f & DERIVED) !== 0) {
   184	                        // if we are assigning to a dirty derived we set it to clean/maybe dirty but we also eagerly execute it to track the dependencies
   185	                        if ((source.f & DIRTY) !== 0) {
   186	                                execute_derived(/** @type {Derived} */ (source));
   187	                        }
   188	                        set_signal_status(source, (source.f & UNOWNED) === 0 ? CLEAN : MAYBE_DIRTY);
   189	                }
   190	
   191	                source.wv = increment_write_version();
   192	
   193	                mark_reactions(source, DIRTY);
   194	
   195	                // It's possible that the current reaction might not have up-to-date dependencies
   196	                // whilst it's actively running. So in the case of ensuring it registers the reaction
   197	                // properly for itself, we need to ensure the current effect actually gets
   198	                // scheduled. i.e: `$effect(() => x++)`
   199	                if (
   200	                        is_runes() &&
   201	                        active_effect !== null &&
   202	                        (active_effect.f & CLEAN) !== 0 &&
   203	                        (active_effect.f & (BRANCH_EFFECT | ROOT_EFFECT)) === 0
   204	                ) {
   205	                        if (untracked_writes === null) {
   206	                                set_untracked_writes([source]);
   207	                        } else {
   208	                                untracked_writes.push(source);
   209	                        }
   210	                }
   211	
   212	                if (DEV && inspect_effects.size > 0) {
   213	                        const inspects = Array.from(inspect_effects);
   214	
   215	                        for (const effect of inspects) {
   216	                                // Mark clean inspect-effects as maybe dirty and then check their dirtiness
   217	                                // instead of just updating the effects - this way we avoid overfiring.
   218	                                if ((effect.f & CLEAN) !== 0) {
   219	                                        set_signal_status(effect, MAYBE_DIRTY);
   220	                                }
   221	                                if (check_dirtiness(effect)) {
   222	                                        update_effect(effect);
   223	                                }
   224	                        }
   225	
   226	                        inspect_effects.clear();
   227	                }
   228	        }
   229	
   230	        return value;
   231	}

   233	/**
   234	 * @template {number | bigint} T
   235	 * @param {Source<T>} source
   236	 * @param {1 | -1} [d]
   237	 * @returns {T}
   238	 */
   239	export function update(source, d = 1) {
   240	        var value = get(source);
   241	        var result = d === 1 ? value++ : value--;
   242	
   243	        set(source, value);
   244	
   245	        // @ts-expect-error
   246	        return result;
   247	}

   255	export function update_pre(source, d = 1) {
   256	        var value = get(source);
   257	
   258	        // @ts-expect-error
   259	        return set(source, d === 1 ? ++value : --value);
   260	}

   262	/**
   263	 * @param {Value} signal
   264	 * @param {number} status should be DIRTY or MAYBE_DIRTY
   265	 * @returns {void}
   266	 */
   267	function mark_reactions(signal, status) {
   268	        var reactions = signal.reactions;
   269	        if (reactions === null) return;
   270	
   271	        var runes = is_runes();
   272	        var length = reactions.length;
   273	
   274	        for (var i = 0; i < length; i++) {
   275	                var reaction = reactions[i];
   276	                var flags = reaction.f;
   277	
   278	                // Skip any effects that are already dirty
   279	                if ((flags & DIRTY) !== 0) continue;
   280	
   281	                // In legacy mode, skip the current effect to prevent infinite loops
   282	                if (!runes && reaction === active_effect) continue;
   283	
   284	                // Inspect effects need to run immediately, so that the stack trace makes sense
   285	                if (DEV && (flags & INSPECT_EFFECT) !== 0) {
   286	                        inspect_effects.add(reaction);
   287	                        continue;
   288	                }
   289	
   290	                set_signal_status(reaction, status);
   291	
   292	                // If the signal a) was previously clean or b) is an unowned derived, then mark it
   293	                if ((flags & (CLEAN | UNOWNED)) !== 0) {
   294	                        if ((flags & DERIVED) !== 0) {
   295	                                mark_reactions(/** @type {Derived} */ (reaction), MAYBE_DIRTY);
   296	                        } else {
   297	                                schedule_effect(/** @type {Effect} */ (reaction));

1. In `runtime.js`, the `get()` function at lines 818-820 checks if `is_destroying_effect` is true and if `old_values.has(signal)`, then it returns the old value from `old_values.get(signal)`.

2. In `sources.js`, the `internal_set()` function at lines 167-171 stores old values when a state changes. If `is_destroying_effect` is true, it stores the NEW value (line 168), otherwise it stores the OLD value (line 170).

3. The issue is that for **derived values**, when they are updated during a teardown (because their dependencies change), the old value is not being preserved. Let's look at `update_derived` in `deriveds.js`:

At lines 175-191 in `deriveds.js`, the `update_derived` function updates the derived value but doesn't preserve the old value in `old_values` map like `internal_set` does for sources.

   261	export function prop(props, key, flags, fallback) {
   262	        var runes = !legacy_mode_flag || (flags & PROPS_IS_RUNES) !== 0;
   263	        var bindable = (flags & PROPS_IS_BINDABLE) !== 0;
   264	        var lazy = (flags & PROPS_IS_LAZY_INITIAL) !== 0;
   265	
   266	        var fallback_value = /** @type {V} */ (fallback);
   267	        var fallback_dirty = true;
   268	
   269	        var get_fallback = () => {
   270	                if (fallback_dirty) {
   271	                        fallback_dirty = false;
   272	
   273	                        fallback_value = lazy
   274	                                ? untrack(/** @type {() => V} */ (fallback))
   275	                                : /** @type {V} */ (fallback);
   276	                }
   277	
   278	                return fallback_value;
   279	        };
   280	
   281	        /** @type {((v: V) => void) | undefined} */
   282	        var setter;
   283	
   284	        if (bindable) {
   285	                // Can be the case when someone does `mount(Component, props)` with `let props = $state({...})`
   286	                // or `createClassComponent(Component, props)`
   287	                var is_entry_props = STATE_SYMBOL in props || LEGACY_PROPS in props;
   288	
   289	                setter =
   290	                        get_descriptor(props, key)?.set ??
   291	                        (is_entry_props && key in props ? (v) => (props[key] = v) : undefined);
   292	        }
   293	
   294	        var initial_value;
   295	        var is_store_sub = false;
   296	
   297	        if (bindable) {
   298	                [initial_value, is_store_sub] = capture_store_binding(() => /** @type {V} */ (props[key]));
   299	        } else {
   300	                initial_value = /** @type {V} */ (props[key]);
   301	        }
   302	
   303	        if (initial_value === undefined && fallback !== undefined) {
   304	                initial_value = get_fallback();
   305	
   306	                if (setter) {
   307	                        if (runes) e.props_invalid_value(key);
   308	                        setter(initial_value);
   309	                }
   310	        }
   311	
   312	        /** @type {() => V} */
   313	        var getter;
   314	
   315	        if (runes) {
   316	                getter = () => {
   317	                        var value = /** @type {V} */ (props[key]);
   318	                        if (value === undefined) return get_fallback();

Now I understand the issue better! Looking at line 369, when a prop has a setter but no direct binding from the parent, it creates a derived (line 369). This derived wraps the prop getter. When the prop is read in an `onDestroy` callback, if that derived has never been read before (because the prop was only written to, not read), it will be uninitialized and return `null`.

// This tests that derived values return the old value when read during effect teardown

const {

    old_values
} = require('"'"'./packages/svelte/src/internal/client/reactivity/sources.js'"'"');

let state_logs = [];
{
    const foo = source(false);
    const bar = source(false);
    
    const eff = effect(() => {
        const foo_val = get(foo);
        const bar_val = get(bar);
        state_logs.push(['"'"'up'"'"', { foo: foo_val, bar: bar_val }]);
        
        return () => {
            const foo_val_teardown = get(foo);
            const bar_val_teardown = get(bar);
            state_logs.push(['"'"'down'"'"', { foo: foo_val_teardown, bar: bar_val_teardown }]);
        };
    });
    
    flushSync();
    console.log('"'"'After first effect run:'"'"', JSON.stringify(state_logs));
    
    set(foo, true);
    set(bar, true);
    flushSync();
    console.log('"'"'After state change:'"'"', JSON.stringify(state_logs));

    const down_log = state_logs[1];
    if (down_log[0] === '"'"'down'"'"' && down_log[1].foo === false && down_log[1].bar === false) {
        console.log('"'"'✓ Test 1 PASSED: $state returns old value in teardown'"'"');
    } else {
        console.log('"'"'✗ Test 1 FAILED: Expected { foo: false, bar: false }, got'"'"', JSON.stringify(down_log[1]));

}

{

        const foo_val = get(foo);
        const bar_val = get(bar);

```javascript
}
```

This checks if we're in a teardown (is_destroying_effect) and if the signal has an old value stored. For sources ($state), the old value is stored when `internal_set` is called. But for deriveds, there's no such mechanism!

Let me check `update_derived` in deriveds.js again:

   171	/**
   172	 * @param {Derived} derived
   173	 * @returns {void}
   174	 */
   175	export function update_derived(derived) {
   176	        var value = execute_derived(derived);
   177	
   178	        if (!derived.equals(value)) {
   179	                derived.v = value;
   180	                derived.wv = increment_write_version();
   181	        }
   182	
   183	        // don't mark derived clean if we're reading it inside a
   184	        // cleanup function, or it will cache a stale value
   185	        if (is_destroying_effect) return;
   186	
   187	        var status =
   188	                (skip_reaction || (derived.f & UNOWNED) !== 0) && derived.deps !== null ? MAYBE_DIRTY : CLEAN;
   189	
   190	        set_signal_status(derived, status);
   191	}
   192

Excellent! Now I've reproduced the second issue. The prop value is `null` when read in onDestroy/teardown when it has a setter but was never read before destruction.

Let me analyze this more carefully. Looking at the `prop` function in props.js at line 369:

```javascript
var d = ((flags & PROPS_IS_IMMUTABLE) !== 0 ? derived : derived_safe_equal)(getter);
```

A derived is created that wraps the prop getter. But if this derived is never read before the teardown, it remains uninitialized with `v: null` (from line 54 in deriveds.js).

Now let's trace through what happens during teardown:
1. When the effect runs teardown, it reads the prop
2. The prop function returns `get(d)` (line 392 in props.js)
3. `get(d)` checks if we're in `is_destroying_effect` mode
4. Since the derived was never evaluated before, it has `v: null`
5. `get` returns `null` instead of evaluating the derived

The issue is that when we're in `is_destroying_effect` mode and we try to read an uninitialized derived, we should still evaluate it to get its actual value, not return the uninitialized `null`.

Let me now understand the first issue better. Let me read the playground link from the PR carefully:

The first issue says: "The latest value, instead of the previous value, is provided in $effect teardown if the state is a $derived"

// Based on the PR description: derived should show previous value in teardown

import { flushSync } from '"'"'./packages/svelte/src/index-client.js'"'"';
import { source, set } from '"'"'./packages/svelte/src/internal/client/reactivity/sources.js'"'"';

    console.log('"'"'  [derived] bar computing, foo ='"'"', val);
    return val * 2;
});

There we go! The derived IS updated BEFORE the effect teardown! Notice:\n1. After `set(foo, 5)`, the derived is marked dirty\n2. When we call `flushSync()`, the derived is recomputed: `[DERIVED COMPUTED] bar = foo * 2 = 5 * 2 = 10`\n3. THEN the effect teardown runs: `[effect1] teardown - bar: 10`\n4. The derived is being updated to the new value BEFORE the effect's teardown runs, so when the teardown tries to read it, it gets the new value instead of the old value.\n\nNow let's understand why `old_values` doesn't have the derived's old value. Looking at `update_derived` in deriveds.js:\n\n```javascript\nexport function update_derived(derived) {\n    var value = execute_derived(derived);\n\n    if (!derived.equals(value)) {\n        derived.v = value;  // Line 179 - directly updates without storing old value\n        derived.wv = increment_write_version();\n    }\n    // ...\n}\n```\n\nThe problem is clear: unlike `internal_set` for sources (which stores the old value in `old_values`), `update_derived` directly updates `derived.v` without preserving the old value.\n\nNow let me look at when effects are updated relative to deriveds. Let me check the `check_dirtiness` function in runtime.js to understand the order:\n\nLines 203-213 in runtime.js show that when checking if a reaction is dirty, it first updates any dirty derived dependencies:\n```javascript\nfor (i = 0; i < length; i++) {\n    dependency = dependencies[i];\n\n    if (check_dirtiness(/** @type {Derived} */ (dependency))) {\n        update_derived(/** @type {Derived} */ (dependency));  // Updates derived FIRST\n    }\n\n    if (dependency.wv > reaction.wv) {\n        return true;\n    }\n}\n```\n\nSo when an effect needs to check if it's dirty, it updates all its derived dependencies first. 2025-12-26 15:01:10,447 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
AHA! There we go! The derived IS updated BEFORE the effect teardown! Notice:
1. After `set(foo, 5)`, the derived is marked dirty
2. When we call `flushSync()`, the derived is recomputed: `[DERIVED COMPUTED] bar = foo * 2 = 5 * 2 = 10`
3. THEN the effect teardown runs: `[effect1] teardown - bar: 10`
4. But it should be reading the OLD value (0), not the NEW value (10)!

So the issue is real! The derived is being updated to the new value BEFORE the effect's teardown runs, so when the teardown tries to read it, it gets the new value instead of the old value.

Now let's understand why `old_values` doesn't have the derived's old value. Looking at `update_derived` in deriveds.js:

```javascript
export function update_derived(derived) {
    var value = execute_derived(derived);

    if (!derived.equals(value)) {
        derived.v = value;  // Line 179 - directly updates without storing old value
        derived.wv = increment_write_version();
    }
    // ...
}
```

The problem is clear: unlike `internal_set` for sources (which stores the old value in `old_values`), `update_derived` directly updates `derived.v` without preserving the old value.

Now let me look at when effects are updated relative to deriveds. Let me check the `check_dirtiness` function in runtime.js to understand the order:

Lines 203-213 in runtime.js show that when checking if a reaction is dirty, it first updates any dirty derived dependencies:
```javascript
for (i = 0; i < length; i++) {
    dependency = dependencies[i];

    if (check_dirtiness(/** @type {Derived} */ (dependency))) {
        update_derived(/** @type {Derived} */ (dependency));  // Updates derived FIRST
    }

    if (dependency.wv > reaction.wv) {
        return true;
    }
}
```

So when an effect needs to check if it's dirty, it updates all its derived dependencies first. That's why the derived gets the new value before the effect's teardown runs.

Now let's fix both issues:

1. **Issue 1**: When `update_derived` updates a derived value, it should store the old value in `old_values` if we're in the process of destroying an effect
2. **Issue 2**: When reading an uninitialized derived during teardown, we should evaluate it instead of returning `null`

Let me implement the fixes:

export function update_derived(derived) {
        var value = execute_derived(derived);

        if (!derived.equals(value)) {
                derived.v = value;
                derived.wv = increment_write_version();
        }

        // don'"'"'t mark derived clean if we'"'"'re reading it inside a

export function update_derived(derived) {
        var value = execute_derived(derived);

        if (!derived.equals(value)) {
                // Store old value in old_values map, similar to how sources do it
                // This ensures that when reading the derived during effect teardown,
                // we can return the previous value instead of the updated value
                if (DEV) {
                        var { old_values } = await import('"'"'./sources.js'"'"');

                                old_values.set(derived, derived.v);

```javascript

        execute_derived(/** @type {Derived} */ (source));
```

This is getting complex. Let me look at what happens when a prop is written to. When we call `checked_prop(true)`, it goes to line 374-384 in props.js:


So it calls `set(d, new_value)` where `d` is the derived created at line 369. The `set` function will:
1. Store the old value in `old_values` (line 170 in sources.js)
2. Update `d.v = value` (line 173)
3. If the signal is a derived and dirty, execute it (lines 183-187)

But here's the issue: when the derived is FIRST created, it has never been read, so it's dirty and uninitialized. When we call `set(d, true)`, it:
1. Stores `old_values.set(d, d.v)` where `d.v` is still `null` (the initial value)
2. Sets `d.v = true`
3. Since `d` is a derived and dirty, calls `execute_derived(d)`
4. `execute_derived(d)` evaluates the getter function and returns the result
5. But this happens inside `internal_set`, so the value from `execute_derived` is not used to update `d.v` again

Let me trace through this more carefully. When `set(d, true)` is called on a derived:

1. Line 164 in sources.js: `if (!source.equals(value))` - checks if value changed
2. Line 165: `var old_value = source.v;` - gets current value (null)
3. Lines 167-171: stores old value in `old_values`

5. Lines 183-189: If it's a derived...

   - But this doesn't update `source.v` again!

- Line 818: `if (is_destroying_effect && old_values.has(d))` - TRUE

Actually, let me think about this differently. The real issue is that when a prop is set for the first time, the old value stored should not be the uninitialized `null`, but rather the value it would have had if it were evaluated (which is the getter result).

Let me check the prop getter again. At line 316-321 in props.js:
```javascript
getter = () => {
    var value = /** @type {V} */ (props[key]);
    if (value === undefined) return get_fallback();
    fallback_dirty = true;
    return value;

```

So the getter reads from `props[key]`. If we call `set(d, true)` on the derived before it's ever been read, and the derived's getter would return `false` (from `parent_props.checked = false`), then the `old_values` should store `false`, not `null`.

The fix should be: when storing the old value of a derived in `old_values`, if the derived has never been computed (i.e., its value is the initial `null` and it has no deps), we should first evaluate it to get its actual value.

Actually, I think the issue is that the prop's derived IS evaluated when we call `set(d, true)` at line 186 in sources.js (`execute_derived`), but the result is not used. Let me check `execute_derived`:

At line 136-169 in deriveds.js, `execute_derived` executes the derived's function and returns the value. But in the `internal_set` function, this returned value is ignored! The derived is just marked as clean/maybe dirty.

So when we call `set(d, true)` on a prop's derived:
1. It stores `old_values.set(d, null)` (the uninitialized value)
2. It sets `d.v = true` (the new value we're setting)
3. If the derived is dirty, it calls `execute_derived(d)` which evaluates the getter and returns the actual prop value (e.g., `false`)
4. But this return value is ignored!
5. So `d.v` remains `true`

Then when we read it during teardown, we get the old value from `old_values` which is `null`.

The real fix is more subtle. The issue is that we're using `set` on a derived to update a prop, but deriveds are supposed to be computed from their dependencies, not set directly. 

Looking at this more, I think the real issue is that when we store the old value in `old_values` for a derived that has never been computed, we're storing the uninitialized `null` instead of the value it would have if it were computed.

export function internal_set(source, value) {
        if (!source.equals(value)) {
                var old_value = source.v;

                // If the source is a derived that has never been computed (v is still null and deps is null),
                // we need to evaluate it to get the actual old value before storing it.
                // This fixes the issue where props with setters but no getters return null in onDestroy.

    console.log('"'"'   [effect body]'"'"');

        teardown_value = checked_prop();
        console.log('"'"'   [teardown] Read value:'"'"', teardown_value);
    };
});

Excellent! The teardown is now being called and it reads the value as `true`! But wait, that's not right either. Let me think about this...

When the effect runs initially (step 7), the teardown hasn't run yet, so `teardown_value` is `null`.

When we trigger the re-run (step 8), the teardown runs and reads `true`. But according to the issue, it should read the PREVIOUS value, not the current value. Actually, I think I misunderstood the issue. Let me re-read the PR description:

> "When a prop has a setter ... but it doesn't have a getter ... the value read during `onDestroy` does not match either the old or the current value of the prop, it's instead read as `null`."

So the issue is that it reads as `null` when it should read as either the old or current value. In my test, after my fix, it reads as `true` (the current value), which is better than `null`!

Let me create a test that more closely matches the scenario in the PR description - where the prop is changed from outside and we read it in onDestroy:

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor create /testbed/test_prop_component.js --file_text '// Test matching the PR description more closely

import { flushSync } from '"'"'./packages/svelte/src/index-client.js'"'"';
import { source, set } from '"'"'./packages/svelte/src/internal/client/reactivity/sources.js'"'"';
import { prop } from '"'"'./packages/svelte/src/internal/client/reactivity/props.js'"'"';
import { effect, component_root } from '"'"'./packages/svelte/src/internal/client/reactivity/effects.js'"'"';
import { get } from '"'"'./packages/svelte/src/internal/client/runtime.js'"'"';
import { PROPS_IS_UPDATED, PROPS_IS_RUNES } from '"'"'./packages/svelte/src/constants.js'"'"';

console.log('"'"'\n=== Test: Prop with setter but no getter, read in onDestroy ==='"'"');

// Simulate parent state
let count = source(0);

// Component that receives a prop
function createChildComponent(checked_value) {
    const props = { checked: checked_value };
    
    // Create prop with PROPS_IS_UPDATED (has setter)
    const checked = prop(props, '"'"'checked'"'"', PROPS_IS_RUNES | PROPS_IS_UPDATED, false);
    
    let ondestroy_value = null;
    
    // Component effect
    const root = component_root(() => {
        // Write to checked (setter usage)
        checked(true);
        
        // onDestroy
        effect(() => {
            return () => {
                ondestroy_value = checked();
                console.log('"'"'   onDestroy - checked:'"'"', ondestroy_value);
            };
        });
    });
    
    return { root, ondestroy_value: () => ondestroy_value };
}

console.log('"'"'\n1. Mount component with checked=false'"'"');
let component = createChildComponent(false);
flushSync();

console.log('"'"'\n2. Unmount component'"'"');
component.root();
flushSync();

let result = component.ondestroy_value();
console.log('"'"'\n3. onDestroy value:'"'"', result);

import { flushSync } from '"'"'./packages/svelte/src/index-client.js'"'"';
import { source, set } from '"'"'./packages/svelte/src/internal/client/reactivity/sources.js'"'"';
import { derived } from '"'"'./packages/svelte/src/internal/client/reactivity/deriveds.js'"'"';
import { effect } from '"'"'./packages/svelte/src/internal/client/reactivity/effects.js'"'"';
import { prop } from '"'"'./packages/svelte/src/internal/client/reactivity/props.js'"'"';
import { get } from '"'"'./packages/svelte/src/internal/client/runtime.js'"'"';
import { PROPS_IS_UPDATED, PROPS_IS_RUNES } from '"'"'./packages/svelte/src/constants.js'"'"';

let tests_passed = 0;
let tests_failed = 0;

function test(name, fn) {
    try {
        fn();
        console.log(`✓ ${name}`);
        tests_passed++;
    } catch (err) {
        console.log(`✗ ${name}`);
        console.log(`  Error: ${err.message}`);
        tests_failed++;
    }
}

console.log('"'"'\n=== Comprehensive Test Suite ===\n'"'"');

// Test 1: $state returns old value in teardown
test('"'"'$state returns old value in teardown'"'"', () => {
    let logs = [];
    const foo = source(0);
    
    const eff = effect(() => {
        const val = get(foo);
        logs.push(['"'"'up'"'"', val]);
        
        return () => {
            logs.push(['"'"'down'"'"', get(foo)]);
        };
    });
    
    flushSync();
    set(foo, 5);
    flushSync();
    
    if (logs[1][0] !== '"'"'down'"'"' || logs[1][1] !== 0) {
        throw new Error(`Expected down with 0, got ${JSON.stringify(logs[1])}`);
    }
});

// Test 2: $derived returns old value in teardown
test('"'"'$derived returns old value in teardown'"'"', () => {
    let logs = [];
    const foo = source(0);
    const bar = derived(() => get(foo) * 2);
    
    const eff = effect(() => {
        const val = get(bar);
        logs.push(['"'"'up'"'"', val]);
        
        return () => {
            logs.push(['"'"'down'"'"', get(bar)]);
        };
    });
    
    flushSync();
    set(foo, 5);
    flushSync();
    
    if (logs[1][0] !== '"'"'down'"'"' || logs[1][1] !== 0) {
        throw new Error(`Expected down with 0, got ${JSON.stringify(logs[1])}`);
    }
});

// Test 3: Nested deriveds return old values in teardown
test('"'"'Nested deriveds return old values in teardown'"'"', () => {
    let logs = [];
    const foo = source(1);
    const bar = derived(() => get(foo) * 2);
    const baz = derived(() => get(bar) + 10);
    
    const eff = effect(() => {
        const val = get(baz);
        logs.push(['"'"'up'"'"', val]);
        
        return () => {
            logs.push(['"'"'down'"'"', get(baz)]);
        };
    });
    
    flushSync();
    set(foo, 5);
    flushSync();
    
    // Initial: foo=1, bar=2, baz=12
    // After: foo=5, bar=10, baz=20
    if (logs[1][0] !== '"'"'down'"'"' || logs[1][1] !== 12) {
        throw new Error(`Expected down with 12, got ${JSON.stringify(logs[1])}`);
    }
});

// Test 4: Prop with setter but no getter returns actual value in onDestroy
test('"'"'Prop with setter returns value in onDestroy'"'"', () => {
    const parent_props = { checked: false };
    const checked_prop = prop(parent_props, '"'"'checked'"'"', PROPS_IS_RUNES | PROPS_IS_UPDATED, false);
    
    let ondestroy_value = null;
    let deps = source(0);
    
    const eff = effect(() => {
        get(deps);
        checked_prop(true); // Write to prop
        
        return () => {
            ondestroy_value = checked_prop(); // Read in teardown
        };
    });
    
    flushSync();
    set(deps, 1);
    flushSync();
    
    if (ondestroy_value === null) {
        throw new Error('"'"'Prop value is null in onDestroy'"'"');
    }
});

// Test 5: Multiple deriveds changing
test('"'"'Multiple deriveds return old values'"'"', () => {
    let logs = [];
    const a = source(1);
    const b = source(10);
    const c = derived(() => get(a) + get(b));
    
    const eff = effect(() => {
        logs.push(['"'"'up'"'"', { a: get(a), b: get(b), c: get(c) }]);
        
        return () => {
            logs.push(['"'"'down'"'"', { a: get(a), b: get(b), c: get(c) }]);
        };
    });
    
    flushSync();
    set(a, 2);
    set(b, 20);
    flushSync();
    
    const down_log = logs[1];
    if (down_log[0] !== '"'"'down'"'"' || down_log[1].a !== 1 || down_log[1].b !== 10 || down_log[1].c !== 11) {
        throw new Error(`Expected old values (a:1, b:10, c:11), got ${JSON.stringify(down_log[1])}`);
    }
});

// Test 6: Derived that'"'"'s read in effect but not in teardown should still work
test('"'"'Derived read in effect works normally'"'"', () => {
    const foo = source(0);
    const bar = derived(() => get(foo) * 2);
    
    let effect_value = null;
    const eff = effect(() => {
        effect_value = get(bar);
    });
    
    flushSync();
    
    if (effect_value !== 0) {
        throw new Error(`Expected 0, got ${effect_value}`);
    }
    
    set(foo, 5);
    flushSync();
    
    if (effect_value !== 10) {
        throw new Error(`Expected 10, got ${effect_value}`);
    }
});

// Test 7: Prop that'"'"'s read before writing should work
test('"'"'Prop read before writing works'"'"', () => {
    const parent_props = { value: 42 };
    const value_prop = prop(parent_props, '"'"'value'"'"', PROPS_IS_RUNES | PROPS_IS_UPDATED, 0);
    
    let initial = value_prop(); // Read first
    
    if (initial !== 42) {
        throw new Error(`Expected 42, got ${initial}`);
    }
    
    value_prop(100); // Then write
    let after = value_prop();
    
    if (after !== 100) {
        throw new Error(`Expected 100, got ${after}`);
    }
});

console.log(`\n=== Results ===`);
console.log(`Passed: ${tests_passed}`);
console.log(`Failed: ${tests_failed}`);

if (tests_failed > 0) {
    process.exit(1);
}
'

2025-12-26 15:12:54,521 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
This test looks like it assigns a function to the prop and then calls it in the teardown. Our fix shouldn't affect this.

Now let me think about potential edge cases for our fixes:

1. **Derived that has never been computed**: Our fix in `internal_set` evaluates it first to get the real old value
2. **Derived that has been computed**: Our fix in `update_derived` stores the old value before updating
3. **Multiple updates in one cycle**: The `old_values` map only stores if the key doesn't exist yet, so multiple updates won't overwrite the original old value

Wait, there's an issue with fix #1. When we check `old_value === null && source.deps === null`, we're assuming that `null` is the uninitialized value. But what if the derived legitimately evaluates to `null`? Let me check the initial value in deriveds.js:

Line 54 in deriveds.js:
```javascript
v: /** @type {V} */ (null),
```

So a newly created derived has `v: null`. But once it's evaluated, even if it returns `null`, it will have `deps` set (not `null` anymore). So our check `old_value === null && source.deps === null` correctly identifies an uninitialized derived!

However, there's still an edge case: what if someone creates a derived that has no dependencies? For example:
```javascript
const d = derived(() => 42);
```

This derived has no dependencies but returns 42. When it's first evaluated, it will have `deps: []` (empty array, not `null`). Let me verify this by checking `update_reaction` in runtime.js...

Looking at line 289-301 in runtime.js, after executing the reaction function, if there are new dependencies, `reaction.deps` is set to `new_deps`. If there are no new dependencies, `new_deps` will be `null`, and the code at line 313-316 handles the case where deps exist but we skipped all of them. So if a derived has no dependencies, `deps` could be `null` or `[]`.

Actually, looking more carefully at line 300, if `new_deps` is not null, it sets `reaction.deps = deps = new_deps`. And `new_deps` starts as `null` (line 266). So if there are no dependencies, `new_deps` stays `null`, and at line 313, if the old `deps` was not null, it would be truncated. But if it was the first evaluation and `deps` was `null`, it stays `null`.

So an evaluated derived with no dependencies will have `deps === null` if it never had any dependencies. This means our check `old_value === null && source.deps === null` would also match a legitimately evaluated constant derived that returns `null`. But wait, if the derived has been evaluated at least once, it won't have `old_value === null` anymore (unless it evaluates to `null`).

Let me reconsider the check. We want to detect: "This derived has never been evaluated". The reliable way to check this is:
- `deps === null` (never been evaluated)
- But also need to check if it's actually dirty/uninitialized

Let me check if there's a better way... Actually, looking at the derived creation in deriveds.js line 30, it has `f: flags` which includes `DIRTY`. So an uninitialized derived is DIRTY. But a derived that has been evaluated and then invalidated is also DIRTY.

The safest check would be: `source.deps === null`. This means the derived has never been executed (even if it would return `null` when executed, after execution it will have `deps` set to either an array or remain `null` but the derived won't be dirty anymore after the first execution).

Let me refine the fix:

                // we need to evaluate it to get the actual old value before storing it.
                // This fixes the issue where props with setters but no getters return null in onDestroy.
